# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes API Server to etcd Storage Write Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a Kubernetes API object write (e.g., Pod creation) flows from the API server handler to etcd storage. Find Go source files implementing: the REST handler, the registry Store, the etcd3 store, the Codec serialization, and the etcd client Put call.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

63-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the Kubernetes API object write chain from the API server handler to etcd storage. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Write Chain Summary

The write flow for a Kubernetes object (e.g., Pod) follows this path:

1. **REST Handler** (`create.go`) - Processes HTTP POST requests and calls the resource's Create method

2. **Generic Registry Store** (`store.go`) - Validates the object using strategies and delegates to underlying storage

3. **Resource-Specific Storage** (`pod/storage/storage.go`) - Uses the generic Store with Pod-specific configuration

4. **etcd3 Storage Backend** (`etcd3/store.go`) - Encodes the object and writes to etcd:
   - Uses `runtime.Encode()` with a Codec to serialize the object to bytes
   - Calls the etcd client's OptimisticPut method

5. **etcd Client OptimisticPut** (`kubernetes/client.go`) - Creates an optimistic transaction with a Put operation

6. **etcd Client OpPut** (`op.go`) - Creates the actual Put operation that gets sent to the etcd server

The complete flow ensures proper validation, serialization (Codec), and atomic writes to etcd with optimistic locking.

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant files, symbols, and a detailed narrative explanation.

finalizers\")\n873: )\n874: \n875: // shouldOrphanDependents returns true if the finalizer for orphaning should be set\n876: // updated for FinalizerOrphanDependents. and e.DeleteStrategy.DefaultGarbageCollectionPolicy.\n880: func shouldOrphanDependents(ctx context.Context, e *Store, accessor metav1.Object, options *metav1.DeleteOptions) bool {\n881: \t// Get orphan\n890: \t\treturn false\n891: \t}\n892: \n893: \t// An explicit policy was set at deletion time, that overrides everything\n894: \t//nolint:staticcheck // SA1019 backwards compatibility\n895: default\n909: \t// validation should make sure the two cases won't be true at the same time.\n910: \tfinalizers := accessor.GetFinalizers()\n911: \tfor _, f := range finalizers {\n912: \t\tswitch f \t\topt(op)\n329: \t}\n330: }\n331: \n332: // OpOption configures Operations like Get, Put, Delete.\n333: type OpOption func(*Op)\n334: \n335: // WithLease attaches a lease ID to a key in 'Put' store revision for 'Get' request.\n345: // Or the start revision of 'Watch' request.\n346: func WithRev(rev int64) OpOption { return func(op *Op) { op.rev = rev } }\n347: \n348: // WithSort specifies the ordering in 'Get' request. It requires\n349: // 'WithRange' and/or 'WithPrefix' to be specified too.\n350: // 'target' specifies the target to sort by: key, version, revisions, value.\n351: // 'order' can be either 'SortNone', 'SortAscend', 'SortDescend'.\n352: func WithSort(target SortTarget, order SortOrder) OpOption {\n353: \treturn func(op *Op) {\n354: \t\tif target == SortByKey && order == SortAscend {\n355: \t\t\t// If order != SortNone, server fetches the entire key-space,\n356: \t\t\t// and then applies the sort and limit, if provided.\n357: \t\t\t// Since by default the server returns results sorted by keys\n358: \t\t\t// in lexicographically ascending order, the client should ignore\n359: \t\t\t// SortOrder if the target is SortByKey.\n360: \t\t\torder = SortNone\n361: \t\t}\n362: \t\top.sort = &SortOption{target, order}\n363: \t}\n364: }\n365: \n366: // GetPrefixRangeEnd gets the range end of the prefix.\n367: // 'Get(foo, WithPrefix())' is equal to 'Get(foo, WithRange(GetPrefixRangeEnd(foo))'.\n368: func GetPrefixRangeEnd(prefix string) string {\n369: \treturn string(getPrefix([]byte(prefix)))\n370: }\n371: \n372: func getPrefix(key []byte) []byte {\n373: \tend := make([]byte, len(key))\n374: \tcopy(end, key)\n375: \tfor i := len(end) - 1; i >= 0; i-- {\n376: \t\tif end[i] < 0xff {\n377: \t\t\tend[i] = end[i] + 1\n378: \t\t\tend = end[:i+1]\n379: \t\t\treturn end\n380: \t\t}\n381: \t}\n382: \t// next prefix does not exist (e.g., 0xffff);\n383: \t// default to WithFromKey policy\n384: \treturn noPrefixEnd\n385: }\n386: \n387: // WithPrefix enables 'Get', 'Delete', or 'Watch' requests to operate\n388: // on the keys with matching prefix. For example, 'Get(foo, WithPrefix())'\n389: // can return 'foo1', 'foo2', and so on.\n390: func WithPrefix() OpOption {\n391: \treturn func(op *Op) {\n392: \t\top.isOptsWithPrefix = true\n393: \t\tif len(op.key) == 0 {\n394: \t\t\top.key, op.end = []byte{0}, []byte{0}\n395: \t\t\treturn\n396: \t\t}\n397: \t\top.end = getPrefix(op.key)\n398: \t}\n399: }\n400: \n401: // WithRange specifies the range of 'Get', 'Delete', 'Watch' requests.\n402: // For example, 'Get' requests with 'WithRange(end)' returns\n403: // the keys in the range [key, end).\n404: // endKey must be lexicographically greater than start key.\n405: func WithRange(endKey string) OpOption {\n406: \treturn func(op *Op) { op.end = []byte(endKey) }\n407: }\n408: \n409: // WithFromKey specifies the range of 'Get', 'Delete', 'Watch' requests\n410: // to be equal or greater than the key in the argument.\n411: func WithFromKey() OpOption {\n412: \treturn func(op *Op) {\n413: \t\tif len(op.key) == 0 {\n414: \t\t\top.key = []byte{0}\n415: \t\t}\n416: \t\top.end = []byte(\"\\x00\")\n417: \t\top.isOptsWithFromKey = true\n418: \t}\n419: }\n420: \n421: // WithSerializable makes 'Get' request serializable. By default,\n422: // it's linearizable. Serializable requests are better for lower latency\n423: // requirement.\n424: func WithSerializable() OpOption {\n425: \treturn func(op *Op) { op.serializable = true }\n426: }\n427: \n428: // }\n432: }\n433: \n434: // WithCountOnly makes the 'Get' request return only the count of keys.\n435: func WithCountOnly() OpOption {\n436: \treturn func(op *Op) { op.countOnly = true }\n437: }\n438: \n439: // WithMinModRev filters out keys for Get with modification revisions less than the given revision.\n440: func WithMinModRev(rev int64) OpOption { return func(op *Op) { op.minModRev = rev } }\n441: \n442: // WithMaxModRev filters out keys for Get with modification revisions greater than the given revision.\n443: func WithMaxModRev(rev int64) OpOption { return func(op *Op) { op.maxModRev = rev } }\n444: \n445: // WithMinCreateRev filters out keys for Get with creation revisions less than the given revision.\n446: func WithMinCreateRev(rev int64) OpOption { return func(op *Op) { op.minCreateRev = rev } }\n447: \n448: // WithMaxCreateRev filters out keys for Get with creation revisions greater than the given revision.\n449: func WithMaxCreateRev(rev int64) OpOption { return func(op *Op) { op.maxCreateRev = rev } }\n450: \n451: // WithFirstCreate gets the key with the oldest creation revision in the request range.\n452: func WithFirstCreate() []OpOption { return
